<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Former_President_and_First_Lady_Carter_wave_from_their_aircraft.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Former_President_and_First_Lady_Carter_wave_from_their_aircraft.jpeg/220px-Former_President_and_First_Lady_Carter_wave_from_their_aircraft.jpeg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Former_President_and_First_Lady_Carter_wave_from_their_aircraft.jpeg/330px-Former_President_and_First_Lady_Carter_wave_from_their_aircraft.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Former_President_and_First_Lady_Carter_wave_from_their_aircraft.jpeg/440px-Former_President_and_First_Lady_Carter_wave_from_their_aircraft.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1970" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Former_President_and_First_Lady_Carter_wave_from_their_aircraft.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Former President and First Lady Carter wave from their aircraft after the <a href="/wiki/First_inauguration_of_Ronald_Reagan" title="First inauguration of Ronald Reagan">inauguration of Ronald Reagan</a> on January 20, 1981.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1981, Carter returned to Georgia to his peanut farm, which he had placed into a <a href="/wiki/Blind_trust" title="Blind trust">blind trust</a> during his presidency to avoid even the appearance of a conflict of interest. He found that the trustees had mismanaged the trust, leaving him more than one million dollars in debt. In the years that followed, he has led an active life, establishing the Carter Center, building his presidential library, teaching at <a href="/wiki/Emory_University" title="Emory University">Emory University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta,_Georgia" title="Atlanta, Georgia" class="mw-redirect">Atlanta, Georgia</a>, and writing numerous books.<sup id="cite_ref-Dyer-2004_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dyer-2004-54"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> He has also contributed to the expansion of Habitat for Humanity, to build affordable housing. Since early September 2012, Carter has been alive longer after leaving the White House than any other U.S. President.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Carter_Center_and_Nobel_Prize">Carter Center and Nobel Prize <span id="Nobel_Peace_Prize"></span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Carter_Center" title="Carter Center">Carter Center</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Living_US_Presidents_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Living_US_Presidents_2009.jpg/220px-Living_US_Presidents_2009.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Living_US_Presidents_2009.jpg/330px-Living_US_Presidents_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Living_US_Presidents_2009.jpg/440px-Living_US_Presidents_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="540" data-file-height="371" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Living_US_Presidents_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
President George W. Bush invited former Presidents George H.W. Bush, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, Jimmy Carter (far right), and President-elect <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> for a meeting and lunch at The White House on January 7, 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Carter has been involved in a variety of national and international public policy, conflict resolution, human rights and charitable causes. In 1982, he established <a href="/wiki/The_Carter_Center" title="The Carter Center" class="mw-redirect">The Carter Center</a> in Atlanta to advance human rights and alleviate human suffering. The non-profit, nongovernmental Center promotes democracy, mediates and prevents conflicts, and monitors the electoral process in support of free and fair elections. It also works to improve global health through the control and <a href="/wiki/Eradication_of_infectious_diseases" title="Eradication of infectious diseases">eradication</a> of diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Guinea_worm_disease" title="Guinea worm disease" class="mw-redirect">Guinea worm disease</a>, <a href="/wiki/Onchocerciasis" title="Onchocerciasis">river blindness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trachoma" title="Trachoma">trachoma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lymphatic_filariasis" title="Lymphatic filariasis">lymphatic filariasis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Schistosomiasis" title="Schistosomiasis">schistosomiasis</a>. It also works to diminish the stigma of mental illnesses and improve nutrition through increased crop production in Africa.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>A major accomplishment of The Carter Center has been the elimination of more than 99&#160;percent of cases of <a href="/wiki/Guinea_worm_disease" title="Guinea worm disease" class="mw-redirect">Guinea worm disease</a>, from an estimated 3.5&#160;million cases in 1986 to 148 reported cases in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The Carter Center has monitored 96 elections in 38 countries since 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> It has worked to resolve conflicts in <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia" title="Bosnia" class="mw-redirect">Bosnia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> and other countries. Carter and the <a href="/wiki/The_Carter_Center" title="The Carter Center" class="mw-redirect">Center</a> support human rights defenders around the world and have intervened with heads of state on their behalf.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 2002, President Carter received the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> for his work "to find peaceful solutions to international conflicts, to advance democracy and human rights, and to promote economic and social development" through The Carter Center.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Three sitting presidents, <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, have received the prize; Carter is unique in receiving the award for his actions after leaving the presidency. He is, along with <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King,_Jr." title="Martin Luther King, Jr.">Martin Luther King, Jr.</a>, one of only two native Georgians to receive the Nobel.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diplomacy">Diplomacy</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_President_Jimmy_Carter_Presidential_Trips.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/US_President_Jimmy_Carter_Presidential_Trips.PNG/300px-US_President_Jimmy_Carter_Presidential_Trips.PNG" width="300" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/US_President_Jimmy_Carter_Presidential_Trips.PNG/450px-US_President_Jimmy_Carter_Presidential_Trips.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/US_President_Jimmy_Carter_Presidential_Trips.PNG/600px-US_President_Jimmy_Carter_Presidential_Trips.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="625" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_President_Jimmy_Carter_Presidential_Trips.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Foreign trips of Jimmy Carter during his presidency</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Korea">North Korea</span></h4>
<p>In 1994, <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> had expelled investigators from the <a href="/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency" title="International Atomic Energy Agency">International Atomic Energy Agency</a> and was threatening to begin processing spent nuclear fuel. In response, then-President Clinton pressured for US sanctions and ordered large amounts of troops and vehicles into the area to brace for war.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Bill Clinton secretly recruited Carter to undertake a peace mission to North Korea,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> under the guise that it was a private mission of Carter's. Clinton saw Carter as a way to let North Korean President <a href="/wiki/Kim_Il-sung" title="Kim Il-sung">Kim Il-sung</a> back down without losing face.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carter negotiated an understanding with Kim Il-sung, but went further and outlined a treaty, which he announced on CNN without the permission of the Clinton White House as a way to force the US into action.</p>
<p>The Clinton Administration signed a later version of the <a href="/wiki/Agreed_Framework" title="Agreed Framework">Agreed Framework</a>, under which North Korea agreed to freeze and ultimately dismantle its current nuclear program and comply with its <a href="/wiki/Nonproliferation" title="Nonproliferation" class="mw-redirect">nonproliferation</a> obligations in exchange for oil deliveries, the construction of two <a href="/wiki/Light_water_reactors" title="Light water reactors" class="mw-redirect">light water reactors</a> to replace its <a href="/wiki/Graphite_moderated_reactors" title="Graphite moderated reactors" class="mw-redirect">graphite reactors</a>, and discussions for eventual diplomatic relations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The agreement was widely hailed at the time as a significant diplomatic achievement.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> However, in December 2002, the <a href="/wiki/Agreed_Framework" title="Agreed Framework">Agreed Framework</a> collapsed as a result of a dispute between the <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush_Administration" title="George W. Bush Administration" class="mw-redirect">George W. Bush Administration</a> and the North Korean government of <a href="/wiki/Kim_Jong-il" title="Kim Jong-il">Kim Jong-il</a>.</p>
<p>In 2001, George W. Bush had taken a confrontational position toward North Korea. And in January 2002, Bush had named North Korea as part of an "<a href="/wiki/Axis_of_Evil" title="Axis of Evil" class="mw-redirect">Axis of Evil</a>". Meanwhile, North Korea began developing the capability to <a href="/wiki/Enriched_uranium" title="Enriched uranium">enrich uranium</a>.</p>
<p>Bush Administration opponents of the <a href="/wiki/Agreed_Framework" title="Agreed Framework">Agreed Framework</a> believed that the North Korean government never intended to give up a nuclear weapons program. However, supporters of the Agreed Framework believed that the agreement could have been successful, had it not been undermined by the Bush Administration.<sup id="cite_ref-commentary10824_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-commentary10824-82"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2010, Carter traveled to North Korea in an attempt to secure the release of <a href="/wiki/Aijalon_Mahli_Gomes" title="Aijalon Mahli Gomes" class="mw-redirect">Aijalon Mahli Gomes</a>. Gomes, a <a href="/wiki/Citizenship_in_the_United_States" title="Citizenship in the United States">U.S. citizen</a>, was sentenced to eight years of hard labor after being found guilty of illegally entering North Korea. Carter successfully secured the release.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_East">Middle East</span></h4>
<p>Carter and experts from The Carter Center assisted unofficial Israeli and Palestinian negotiators in designing a model agreement for peace—called the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Accord_(2003)" title="Geneva Accord (2003)" class="mw-redirect">Geneva Accord</a>—in 2002–2003.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carter has also in recent years become a frequent critic of Israel's policies in <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, at the UK <a href="/wiki/Hay_Festival" title="Hay Festival">Hay Festival</a>, Carter stated that <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> has at least 150 <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons" title="Nuclear weapons" class="mw-redirect">nuclear weapons</a>. He expressed his support for Israel as a country, but criticized its domestic and foreign policy; "One of the greatest human rights crimes on earth is the starvation and imprisonment of 1.6m Palestinians," said Carter.<sup id="cite_ref-Israel150_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel150-87"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>He mentioned statistics showing nutritional intake of some Palestinian children was below that of the children of Sub-Saharan Africa and described the European position on Israel as "<a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/supine" class="extiw" title="wikt:supine">supine</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Israel150_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel150-87"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2008, the London-based Arabic newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Al-Hayat" title="Al-Hayat">Al-Hayat</a></i> reported that Carter met with exiled <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Khaled_Mashaal" title="Khaled Mashaal" class="mw-redirect">Khaled Mashaal</a> on his visit to <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>. The Carter Center initially did not confirm nor deny the story. The <a href="/wiki/US_State_Department" title="US State Department" class="mw-redirect">US State Department</a> considers Hamas a terrorist organization.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> Within this Mid-East trip, Carter also laid a wreath on the grave of <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ramallah" title="Ramallah">Ramallah</a> on April 14, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> Carter said on April 23 that neither <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a> nor anyone else in the State Department had warned him against meeting with Hamas leaders during his trip.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> Carter spoke to Mashaal on several matters, including "formulas for prisoner exchange to obtain the release of Corporal <a href="/wiki/Gilad_Shalit" title="Gilad Shalit">Shalit</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2007, while arguing that the United States should directly talk to Iran, Carter again stated that Israel has 150 nuclear weapons in its arsenal.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2008, Carter visited Damascus again, where he met with Syrian President <a href="/wiki/Bashar_al-Assad" title="Bashar al-Assad">Bashar al-Assad</a>, and the Hamas leadership. During his visit he gave an exclusive interview to <i><a href="/wiki/Forward_Magazine" title="Forward Magazine">Forward Magazine</a></i>, the first ever interview for any American president, current or former, with a Syrian media outlet.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carter visited with three officials from Hamas who have been living at the International Red Cross office in <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> since July 2010. Israel believes that these three Hamas legislators had a role in the 2006 kidnapping of Israeli soldier <a href="/wiki/Gilad_Shalit" title="Gilad Shalit">Gilad Shalit</a>, and has a deportation order set for them.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2014, Carter was joined by <a href="/wiki/Mary_Robinson" title="Mary Robinson">Mary Robinson</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2014_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict" title="2014 Israel–Gaza conflict">2014 Israel–Gaza conflict</a> with the pair pressing for the inclusion of Hamas as an actor in peace talks with Israel, recognition of the group as a legitimate political entity, and the lifting of the siege of Gaza. The two <a href="/wiki/The_Elders_(organization)" title="The Elders (organization)">Elders</a>, in an op-ed article in <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Policy_(magazine)" title="Foreign Policy (magazine)" class="mw-redirect"><i>Foreign Policy</i></a>, noted the recent unity deal between Hamas and Fatah when Hamas agreed with the Palestinian Authority to denounce violence, recognize Israel and adhere to past agreements, saying it presented an opportunity. Carter and Robinson called on the UN Security Council to act on what they described as the inhumane conditions in Gaza, and mandate an end to the siege.<sup id="cite_ref-CarterRobinson_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CarterRobinson-96"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ranjit_Bhaskar_Juba,_jan_9,_2011042_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Ranjit_Bhaskar_Juba%2C_jan_9%2C_2011042_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/220px-Ranjit_Bhaskar_Juba%2C_jan_9%2C_2011042_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Ranjit_Bhaskar_Juba%2C_jan_9%2C_2011042_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/330px-Ranjit_Bhaskar_Juba%2C_jan_9%2C_2011042_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Ranjit_Bhaskar_Juba%2C_jan_9%2C_2011042_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/440px-Ranjit_Bhaskar_Juba%2C_jan_9%2C_2011042_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ranjit_Bhaskar_Juba,_jan_9,_2011042_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Carter leads an observer mission at <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/South_Sudanese_independence_referendum,_2011" title="South Sudanese independence referendum, 2011">referendum on independence</a>, January 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Carter held summits in Egypt and <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a> in 1995–1996 to address violence in the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">Great Lakes region</a> of Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carter played a key role in negotiation of the <a href="/wiki/Nairobi_Agreement,_1999" title="Nairobi Agreement, 1999">Nairobi Agreement</a> in 1999 between Sudan and <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On June 18, 2007, Carter, accompanied by his wife, arrived in Dublin, Ireland, for talks with President <a href="/wiki/Mary_McAleese" title="Mary McAleese">Mary McAleese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bertie_Ahern" title="Bertie Ahern">Bertie Ahern</a> concerning human rights. On June 19, Carter attended and spoke at the annual Human Rights Forum at <a href="/wiki/Croke_Park" title="Croke Park">Croke Park</a>. An agreement between Irish Aid and The Carter Center was also signed on this day.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Americas">Americas</span></h4>
<p>Carter led a mission to <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> in 1994 with Senator <a href="/wiki/Sam_Nunn" title="Sam Nunn">Sam Nunn</a> and former chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff" title="Joint Chiefs of Staff">Joint Chiefs of Staff</a> <a href="/wiki/Colin_Powell" title="Colin Powell">General Colin Powell</a> to avert a US-led multinational invasion and restore to power Haiti's democratically elected president, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Bertrand_Aristide" title="Jean-Bertrand Aristide">Jean-Bertrand Aristide</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carter visited <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> in May 2002 and had full discussions with <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_government" title="Cuban government" class="mw-redirect">Cuban government</a>. He was allowed to address the Cuban public uncensored on national television and radio with a speech that he wrote and presented in Spanish. In the speech, he called on the US to end "an ineffective 43-year-old <a href="/wiki/United_States_embargo_against_Cuba" title="United States embargo against Cuba">economic embargo</a>" and on Castro to hold free elections, improve human rights, and allow greater <a href="/wiki/Civil_liberties" title="Civil liberties">civil liberties</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> He met with political dissidents; visited the <a href="/wiki/AIDS" title="AIDS" class="mw-redirect">AIDS</a> sanitarium, a medical school, a <a href="/wiki/Biotech" title="Biotech" class="mw-redirect">biotech</a> facility, an agricultural production cooperative, and a school for disabled children; and threw a pitch for an all-star baseball game in <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>. The visit made Carter the first President of the United States, in or out of office, to visit the island since the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_revolution" title="Cuban revolution" class="mw-redirect">Cuban revolution</a> of 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carter observed the <a href="/wiki/Venezuelan_recall_referendum,_2004" title="Venezuelan recall referendum, 2004">Venezuela recall elections</a> on August 15, 2004. European Union observers had declined to participate, saying too many restrictions were put on them by the <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Chávez">Hugo Chávez</a> administration.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> A record number of voters turned out to defeat the recall attempt with a 59&#160;percent "no" vote.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> The Carter Center stated that the process "suffered from numerous irregularities," but said it did not observe or receive "evidence of fraud that would have changed the outcome of the vote".<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> On the afternoon of August 16, 2004, the day after the vote, Carter and <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a> (OAS) <a href="/wiki/Secretary_General_of_the_Organization_of_American_States" title="Secretary General of the Organization of American States">Secretary General</a> <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9sar_Gaviria" title="César Gaviria">César Gaviria</a> gave a joint press conference in which they endorsed the preliminary results announced by the National Electoral Council. The monitors' findings "coincided with the partial returns announced today by the National Elections Council," said Carter, while Gaviria added that the OAS electoral observation mission's members had "found no element of fraud in the process." Directing his remarks at opposition figures who made claims of "widespread fraud" in the voting, Carter called on all Venezuelans to "accept the results and work together for the future".<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Penn,_Schoen_%26_Berland" title="Penn, Schoen &amp; Berland" class="mw-redirect">Penn, Schoen &amp; Berland</a> Associates (PSB) <a href="/wiki/Exit_poll" title="Exit poll">exit poll</a> had predicted that Chávez would lose by 20&#160;percent; when the election results showed him to have won by 20&#160;percent, <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Schoen" title="Douglas Schoen">Douglas Schoen</a> commented, "I think it was a massive fraud".<sup id="cite_ref-Barone_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barone-106"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>US News &amp; World Report</i> offered an analysis of the polls, indicating "very good reason to believe that the [Penn, Schoen &amp; Berland] exit poll had the result right, and that Chávez's election officials&#160;– and Carter and the American media&#160;– got it wrong." The exit poll and the Venezuela government's control of election machines became the basis of claims of election fraud. However an <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> report states that Penn, Schoen &amp; Berland used volunteers from pro-recall organization <a href="/wiki/S%C3%BAmate" title="Súmate">Súmate</a> for fieldwork, and its results contradicted five other opposition exit polls.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Following <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>'s severing of ties with <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> in March 2008, Carter brokered a deal for agreement between the countries' respective presidents on the restoration of low-level <a href="/wiki/Colombia-Ecuador_relations" title="Colombia-Ecuador relations" class="mw-redirect">diplomatic relations</a> announced June 8, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Vietnam">Vietnam</span></h4>
<p>On November 18, 2009, Carter visited Vietnam to build houses for the poor. The one-week program, known as Jimmy and Rosalynn Carter Work Project 2009, built 32 houses in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dong_Xa_(Hai_Duong)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dong Xa (Hai Duong) (page does not exist)">Dong Xa</a> village, in the northern province of <a href="/wiki/H%E1%BA%A3i_D%C6%B0%C6%A1ng_Province" title="H?i D??ng Province">H?i D??ng</a>. The project launch was scheduled for November 14, according to the news source which quoted the Ministry of Foreign Affairs spokeswoman <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nguyen_Phuong_Nga&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nguyen Phuong Nga (page does not exist)">Nguyen Phuong Nga</a>. Administered by the non-governmental and non-profit <a href="/wiki/Habitat_for_Humanity_International" title="Habitat for Humanity International" class="mw-redirect">Habitat for Humanity International</a> (HFHI), the annual program of 2009 would build and repair 166 homes in Vietnam and some other Asian countries with the support of nearly 3,000 volunteers around the world, the organization said on its website. HFHI has worked in Vietnam since 2001 to provide low-cost housing, water, and sanitation solutions for the poor. It has worked in provinces like <a href="/wiki/Ti%E1%BB%81n_Giang_Province" title="Ti?n Giang Province">Ti?n Giang</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C4%90%E1%BB%93ng_Nai_Province" title="??ng Nai Province">??ng Nai</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh_City" title="Ho Chi Minh City">Ho Chi Minh City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Elders">The Elders</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Elders_(organization)" title="The Elders (organization)">The Elders (organization)</a></div>
<p>On July 18, 2007, Carter joined <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a> in Johannesburg, South Africa, to announce his participation in <a href="/wiki/The_Elders_(organization)" title="The Elders (organization)">The Elders</a>, a group of independent global leaders who work together on peace and human rights issues.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> The Elders work globally, on thematic as well as geographically specific subjects. The organization's priority issue areas include the <a href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict" class="mw-redirect">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Peninsula" title="Korean Peninsula">Korean Peninsula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women's rights">equality for girls and women</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carter has been actively involved in the work of The Elders, participating in visits to <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Peninsula" title="Korean Peninsula">Korean Peninsula</a>, and the Middle East, among others<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> In October 2007, Carter toured <a href="/wiki/Darfur" title="Darfur">Darfur</a> with several of the Elders, including <a href="/wiki/Desmond_Tutu" title="Desmond Tutu">Desmond Tutu</a>. Sudanese security prevented him from visiting a Darfuri tribal leader, leading to a heated exchange.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> He returned to Sudan with fellow Elder <a href="/wiki/Lakhdar_Brahimi" title="Lakhdar Brahimi">Lakhdar Brahimi</a> in May 2012 as part of The Elders' efforts to encourage the presidents of Sudan and South Sudan to return to negotiations, and highlight the impact of the conflict on civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2008, President Carter, former UN Secretary General <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gra%C3%A7a_Machel" title="Graça Machel">Graça Machel</a>, wife of Nelson Mandela, were stopped from entering <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>, to inspect the human rights situation, by President <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mugabe" title="Robert Mugabe">Robert Mugabe</a>'s government. The Elders instead made their assessment from South Africa, meeting with Zimbabwe– and South Africa-based leaders from politics, business, international organisations and civil society in Johannesburg.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_of_U.S._policy">Criticism of U.S. policy</span></h3>
<p>In 2001, Carter criticized President Bill Clinton's controversial <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_pardoned_or_granted_clemency_by_the_President_of_the_United_States" title="List of people pardoned or granted clemency by the President of the United States">pardon</a> of <a href="/wiki/Marc_Rich" title="Marc Rich">Marc Rich</a>, calling it "disgraceful" and suggesting that Rich's financial contributions to the Democratic Party were a factor in Clinton's action.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2005, Carter urged the closing of the <a href="/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay_detention_camp" title="Guantanamo Bay detention camp">Guantanamo Bay Prison</a> in Cuba, which has been a focal point for recent claims of <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_abuse" title="Prisoner abuse">prisoner abuse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2006, Carter was interviewed on the BBC's current affairs program <i><a href="/wiki/Newsnight" title="Newsnight">Newsnight</a></i>, voicing his concern at the increasing influence of the <a href="/wiki/Christian_right" title="Christian right">Religious Right</a> on US politics.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2009, Carter put weight behind allegations by <a href="/wiki/Venezuelan_President" title="Venezuelan President" class="mw-redirect">Venezuelan President</a> <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Chávez">Hugo Chávez</a>, pertaining to United States involvement in the <a href="/wiki/2002_Venezuelan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="2002 Venezuelan coup d'état attempt">2002 Venezuelan coup d'état attempt</a> by a <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">civilian-military junta</a>, saying that Washington knew about the coup and may have taken part.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On June 16, 2011, the 40th anniversary of <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a>'s official declaration of America's <a href="/wiki/War_on_Drugs" title="War on Drugs">War on Drugs</a>, Carter wrote an <a href="/wiki/Op-ed" title="Op-ed">op-ed</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> urging the United States and the rest of the world to "Call Off the Global War on Drugs",<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> explicitly endorsing the initiative released by the <a href="/wiki/Global_Commission_on_Drug_Policy" title="Global Commission on Drug Policy">Global Commission on Drug Policy</a> earlier that month and quoting a message he gave to Congress in 1977 saying that "[p]enalties against possession of a drug should not be more damaging to an individual than the use of the drug itself."</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticisms_of_George_W._Bush">Criticisms of George W. Bush</span></h4>
<p>Carter has also criticized the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_George_W._Bush" title="Presidency of George W. Bush">presidency of George W. Bush</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a>. In a 2003 <a href="/wiki/Op-ed" title="Op-ed">op-ed</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, Carter warned against the consequences of a war in Iraq and urged restraint in use of military force.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> In March 2004, Carter condemned <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> for waging an unnecessary war "based upon lies and misinterpretations" to oust <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a>. In August 2006, Carter criticized Blair for being "subservient" to the Bush administration and accused Blair of giving unquestioning support to Bush's Iraq policies.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> In a May 2007 interview with the <i><a href="/wiki/Arkansas_Democrat-Gazette" title="Arkansas Democrat-Gazette">Arkansas Democrat-Gazette</a></i>, he said, "I think as far as the adverse impact on the nation around the world, this administration has been the worst in history," when it comes to foreign affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Two days after the quote was published, Carter told <a href="/wiki/Today_(NBC_program)" title="Today (NBC program)" class="mw-redirect">NBC's Today</a> that the "worst in history" comment was "careless or misinterpreted," and that he "wasn't comparing this administration with other administrations back through history, but just with President Nixon's."<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> The day after the "worst in history" comment was published, <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> spokesman <a href="/wiki/Tony_Fratto" title="Tony Fratto">Tony Fratto</a> said that Carter had become "increasingly irrelevant with these kinds of comments."<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On May 19, 2007, Blair made his final visit to Iraq before stepping down as <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">British Prime Minister</a>, and Carter criticized him afterward. Carter told the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> that Blair was "apparently subservient" to Bush and criticized him for his "blind support" for the Iraq war.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc080705_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc080705-129"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Carter described Blair's actions as "abominable" and stated that the British Prime Minister's "almost undeviating support for the ill-advised policies of President Bush in Iraq have been a major tragedy for the world." Carter said he believes that had Blair distanced himself from the Bush administration during the run-up to the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">invasion of Iraq in 2003</a>, it might have made a crucial difference to American political and public opinion, and consequently the invasion might not have gone ahead. Carter states that "one of the defenses of the Bush administration&#160;... has been, okay, we must be more correct in our actions than the world thinks because Great Britain is backing us. So I think the combination of Bush and Blair giving their support to this tragedy in Iraq has strengthened the effort and has made the opposition less effective, and prolonged the war and increased the tragedy that has resulted." Carter expressed his hope that Blair's successor, <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Brown" title="Gordon Brown">Gordon Brown</a>, would be "less enthusiastic" about Bush's Iraq policy.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc080705_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc080705-129"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Due to his status as former President, Carter was a <a href="/wiki/Superdelegate" title="Superdelegate">superdelegate</a> to the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Democratic_National_Convention" title="Democratic National Convention">Democratic National Convention</a>. Carter announced his endorsement of Senator (now president) Barack Obama. Speaking to the Syrian English monthly <i><a href="/wiki/Forward_Magazine" title="Forward Magazine">Forward Magazine</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, Carter was asked to give one word that came to mind when mentioning President George W. Bush. His answer was: the end of a very disappointing administration. His reaction to mentioning Barack Obama was: honesty, intelligence, and politically adept.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticisms_of_Barack_Obama">Criticisms of Barack Obama</span></h4>
<p>Carter has criticized the Obama administration for its use of <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">drone</a> strikes against suspected terrorists. Carter also said that he disagrees with President Obama's decision to keep the <a href="/wiki/Guant%C3%A1namo_Bay_detention_camp" title="Guantánamo Bay detention camp" class="mw-redirect">Guantánamo Bay detention camp</a> open, saying that the inmates "have been tortured by <a href="/wiki/Waterboarding" title="Waterboarding">waterboarding</a> more than 100 times or intimidated with semiautomatic weapons, power drills or threats to sexually assault their mothers." He claimed that the U.S. government had no moral leadership, and was committing human rights violations, and is no longer "the global champion of human rights".<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2013, Carter expressed his criticism of current federal surveillance programs as disclosed by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Snowden" title="Edward Snowden">Edward Snowden</a> indicating that "America has no functioning democracy at this moment."<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Author">Author</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter_bibliography" title="Jimmy Carter bibliography">Jimmy Carter bibliography</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Jimmy_Carter_at_Quail_Ridge_Books-Raleigh_NC-jmturner-2014-04-02.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/President_Jimmy_Carter_at_Quail_Ridge_Books-Raleigh_NC-jmturner-2014-04-02.jpeg/220px-President_Jimmy_Carter_at_Quail_Ridge_Books-Raleigh_NC-jmturner-2014-04-02.jpeg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/President_Jimmy_Carter_at_Quail_Ridge_Books-Raleigh_NC-jmturner-2014-04-02.jpeg/330px-President_Jimmy_Carter_at_Quail_Ridge_Books-Raleigh_NC-jmturner-2014-04-02.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/President_Jimmy_Carter_at_Quail_Ridge_Books-Raleigh_NC-jmturner-2014-04-02.jpeg/440px-President_Jimmy_Carter_at_Quail_Ridge_Books-Raleigh_NC-jmturner-2014-04-02.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Jimmy_Carter_at_Quail_Ridge_Books-Raleigh_NC-jmturner-2014-04-02.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jimmy Carter at a book signing in Raleigh, NC on April 2, 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Carter has been a prolific author in his post-presidency, writing 21 of his 23 books. Among these is one he co-wrote with his wife, <a href="/wiki/Rosalynn_Carter" title="Rosalynn Carter">Rosalynn</a>, and a children's book illustrated by his daughter, <a href="/wiki/Amy_Carter" title="Amy Carter">Amy</a>. They cover a variety of topics, including humanitarian work, aging, religion, human rights, and poetry.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Palestine:_Peace_Not_Apartheid"><i>Palestine: Peace Not Apartheid</i></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Palestine:_Peace_Not_Apartheid" title="Palestine: Peace Not Apartheid">Palestine: Peace Not Apartheid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commentary_on_Palestine:_Peace_Not_Apartheid" title="Commentary on Palestine: Peace Not Apartheid">Commentary on Palestine: Peace Not Apartheid</a></div>
<div class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Israel_and_the_apartheid_analogy" title="Israel and the apartheid analogy">Israel and the apartheid analogy</a></div>
<p>In a 2007 speech to Brandeis University, Carter stated: "I have spent a great deal of my adult life trying to bring peace to Israel and its neighbors, based on justice and righteousness for the Palestinians. These are the underlying purposes of my new book."<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In his book <i><a href="/wiki/Palestine:_Peace_Not_Apartheid" title="Palestine: Peace Not Apartheid">Palestine: Peace Not Apartheid</a></i>, published in November 2006, Carter states:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Israel's continued control and colonization of Palestinian land have been the primary obstacles to a comprehensive peace agreement in the Holy Land.<sup id="cite_ref-excerpt_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-excerpt-135"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>He declares that Israel's current policies in the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_territories" title="Palestinian territories">Palestinian territories</a> constitute "a system of <a href="/wiki/Crime_of_apartheid" title="Crime of apartheid">apartheid</a>, with two peoples occupying the same land, but completely separated from each other, with Israelis totally dominant and suppressing violence by depriving Palestinians of their basic human rights."<sup id="cite_ref-excerpt_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-excerpt-135"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> In an Op-Ed titled "Speaking Frankly about Israel and Palestine," published in the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> and other newspapers, Carter states:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The ultimate purpose of my book is to present facts about the Middle East that are largely unknown in America, to precipitate discussion and to help restart peace talks (now absent for six years) that can lead to permanent peace for Israel and its neighbors. Another hope is that Jews and other Americans who share this same goal might be motivated to express their views, even publicly, and perhaps in concert. I would be glad to help with that effort.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-136"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>While some&#160;– such as a former Special Rapporteur for both the United Nations Commission on Human Rights and the International Law Commission, as well as a member of the Israeli Knesset&#160;– have praised Carter for speaking frankly about Palestinians in <a href="/wiki/Israeli-occupied_territories" title="Israeli-occupied territories">Israeli occupied lands</a>, others&#160;– including the envoy to the Middle East under Clinton, as well as the first director of the Carter Center<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup>&#160;– have accused him of anti-Israeli bias. Specifically, these critics have alleged significant factual errors, omissions and misstatements in the book.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The 2007 documentary film, <i><a href="/wiki/Man_from_Plains" title="Man from Plains">Man from Plains</a></i>, follows President Carter during his tour for the controversial book and other humanitarian efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2009, Carter apologized for any words or deeds that may have upset the Jewish community in an open letter meant to improve an often tense relationship. He said he was offering an <i>Al Het</i>, a prayer said on <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur" title="Yom Kippur">Yom Kippur</a>, the Jewish Day of Atonement.<sup id="cite_ref-apology_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apology-142"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Involvement_with_Bank_of_Credit_and_Commerce_International">Involvement with Bank of Credit and Commerce International</span></h3>
<p>After Carter left the presidency, his interest in the developing countries led him to having a close relationship with <a href="/wiki/Agha_Hasan_Abedi" title="Agha Hasan Abedi">Agha Hasan Abedi</a>, the founder of <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Credit_and_Commerce_International" title="Bank of Credit and Commerce International">Bank of Credit and Commerce International</a> (BCCI). Abedi was a Pakistani, whose bank had offices and business in a large number of developing countries. He was introduced to Carter in 1982 by Bert Lance, one of Carter's closest friends. (Unknown to Carter, BCCI had secretly purchased an interest in 1978 in National Bank of Georgia, which had previously been run by Lance and had made loans to Carter's peanut business.) Abedi made generous donations to the <a href="/wiki/Carter_Center" title="Carter Center">Carter Center</a> and the Global 2000 Project. Abedi also traveled with Carter to at least seven countries in connection with Carter's charitable activities. The main purpose of Abedi's association with Carter was not charitable activities, but to enhance BCCI's influence, in order to open more offices and develop more business. In 1991, BCCI was seized by regulators, amid allegations of criminal activities, including illegally having control of several U.S. banks. Just prior to the seizure, Carter began to disassociate himself from Abedi and the bank.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012_Presidential_race">2012 Presidential race</span></h3>
<p>Despite being a Democrat, Carter endorsed former Massachusetts governor Mitt Romney in the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)_presidential_primaries,_2012" title="Republican Party (United States) presidential primaries, 2012" class="mw-redirect">Republican party 2012 Presidential primary</a> in mid-September 2011, not because he supported Romney, but because he felt Obama's re-election bid would be strengthened in a race against Romney.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> Carter added that he thought Mitt Romney would lose in a match up against Obama and that he supported the president's re-election.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carter addressed the Democratic National Convention in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> by videotape, and did not attend the convention in person.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_activities">Other activities</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FordNixonBushReaganCarter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/FordNixonBushReaganCarter.jpg/220px-FordNixonBushReaganCarter.jpg" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/FordNixonBushReaganCarter.jpg/330px-FordNixonBushReaganCarter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/FordNixonBushReaganCarter.jpg/440px-FordNixonBushReaganCarter.jpg 2x" data-file-width="706" data-file-height="560" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FordNixonBushReaganCarter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Carter (far right) in 1991 with President <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a> and former Presidents Gerald Ford, Richard Nixon, and Ronald Reagan at the dedication of the Reagan Presidential Library</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Carter has participated in many ceremonial events such as the opening of his own presidential library and those of Presidents Ronald Reagan, George H. W. Bush, and Bill Clinton. He has also participated in many forums, lectures, panels, funerals and other events. Carter delivered a eulogy at the funeral of <a href="/wiki/Coretta_Scott_King" title="Coretta Scott King">Coretta Scott King</a> and, most recently, at the <a href="/wiki/Death_and_state_funeral_of_Gerald_Ford" title="Death and state funeral of Gerald Ford">funeral of his former political rival, but later his close, personal friend and diplomatic collaborator, Gerald Ford</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>President Jimmy Carter serves as an Honorary Chair for the <a href="/wiki/World_Justice_Project" title="World Justice Project">World Justice Project</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Justice_Project" title="World Justice Project">World Justice Project</a> works to lead a global, multidisciplinary effort to strengthen the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_Law" title="Rule of Law" class="mw-redirect">Rule of Law</a> for the development of communities of opportunity and equity.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carter serves as Honorary Chair for the <a href="/wiki/Continuity_of_Government_Commission" title="Continuity of Government Commission">Continuity of Government Commission</a> (he was co-chair with <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">Gerald Ford</a> until the latter's death). The Commission recommends improvements to <a href="/wiki/Continuity_of_government" title="Continuity of government">continuity of government</a> measures for the federal government.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_views">Personal views</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abortion">Abortion</span></h3>
<p>Although "personally opposed" to abortion, after the landmark <a href="/wiki/US_Supreme_Court" title="US Supreme Court" class="mw-redirect">US Supreme Court</a> decision <i><a href="/wiki/Roe_v._Wade" title="Roe v. Wade">Roe v. Wade</a></i>, 410 US 113 (1973), Carter supported legalized abortion.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> As president, he did not support increased federal funding for abortion services. He was criticized by the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_Liberties_Union" title="American Civil Liberties Union">American Civil Liberties Union</a> for not doing enough to find alternatives.<sup id="cite_ref-strategy_campaigning_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strategy_campaigning-150"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In a March 29, 2012 interview with <a href="/wiki/Laura_Ingraham" title="Laura Ingraham">Laura Ingraham</a>, Carter expressed his current view of <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">abortion</a> and his wish to see the Democratic Party becoming more <a href="/wiki/Pro-life" title="Pro-life" class="mw-redirect">pro-life</a>: "I never have believed that <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus Christ</a> would approve of abortions and that was one of the problems I had when I was president having to uphold <a href="/wiki/Roe_v._Wade" title="Roe v. Wade">Roe v. Wade</a> and I did everything I could to minimize the need for abortions. I made it easy to adopt children for instance who were unwanted and also initiated the program called Women and Infant Children or <a href="/wiki/WIC" title="WIC">WIC</a> program that's still in existence now. But except for the times when a mother's life is in danger or when a pregnancy is caused by rape or incest I would certainly not or never have approved of any abortions. I've signed a public letter calling for the Democratic Party at the next convention to espouse my position on abortion which is to minimize the need, requirement for abortion and limit it only to women whose life [<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a>?</i>] are in danger or who are pregnant as a result of rape or incest. I think if the Democratic Party would adopt that policy that would be acceptable to a lot of people who are now estranged from our party because of the abortion issue."<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_penalty">Death penalty</span></h3>
<p>During his presidential campaigns, he expressed his opposition to the death penalty, as had George McGovern. Two successive nominees, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Mondale" title="Walter Mondale">Walter Mondale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Dukakis" title="Michael Dukakis">Michael Dukakis</a>, also opposed the death penalty.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> Carter is known for his strong opposition to the death penalty; in his <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> lecture, he urged "prohibition of the death penalty".<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> Carter has continued to speak out against the death penalty in the US and abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In a letter to the Governor of New Mexico, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Richardson" title="Bill Richardson">Bill Richardson</a>, Carter urged the governor to sign a bill to eliminate the death penalty and institute life in prison without parole instead. New Mexico abolished the <a href="/wiki/Death_penalty" title="Death penalty" class="mw-redirect">death penalty</a> in 2009. Carter wrote: "As you know, the United States is one of the few countries, along with nations such as Saudi Arabia, China, and Cuba, which still carry out the death penalty despite the ongoing tragedy of wrongful conviction and gross racial and class-based disparities that make impossible the fair implementation of this ultimate punishment."<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, Carter wrote an <a href="/wiki/Op-ed" title="Op-ed">op-ed</a> in the LA <i>Times</i> supporting passage of a state referendum which would have ended the death penalty. He opened the article: "The process for administering the death penalty in the United States is broken beyond repair, and it is time to choose a more effective and moral alternative. California voters will have the opportunity to do this on election day."<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carter has also called for commutations of death sentences for many death-row inmates, including Brian K. Baldwin (executed in 1999 in <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Foster" title="Kenneth Foster">Kenneth Foster</a> (sentence in <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> commuted in 2007)<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Troy_Anthony_Davis" title="Troy Anthony Davis" class="mw-redirect">Troy Anthony Davis</a> (executed in Georgia in 2011).<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Equality_for_women">Equality for women</span></h3>
<p>In October 2000, Carter, a third-generation Southern Baptist, announced that he was severing connections to the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a> over its opposition to women as pastors. What led Carter to take this action was a doctrinal statement by the Convention, adopted in June 2000, advocating a <a href="/wiki/Biblical_literalism" title="Biblical literalism">literal interpretation of the Bible</a>. This statement followed a position of the Convention two years previously advocating the submission of wives to their husbands. Carter described the reason for his decision as due to: "an increasing inclination on the part of Southern Baptist Convention leaders to be more rigid on what is a Southern Baptist and exclusionary of accommodating those who differ from them." <i>The New York Times</i> called Carter's action "the highest-profile defection yet from the Southern Baptist Convention."<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In subsequent years, Carter has joined with other world leaders who have spoken out about the subjugation of women by religious and other institutions. On July 15, 2009, Carter wrote an opinion piece about equality for women in which he stated that he chooses equality for women over the dictates of the leadership of what has been a lifetime religious commitment. He said that the view that women are inferior is not confined to one faith, "nor, tragically does its influence stop at the walls of the church, mosque, synagogue or temple." Carter stated:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The truth is that male religious leaders have had—and still have—an option to interpret holy teachings either to exalt or subjugate women. They have, for their own selfish ends, overwhelmingly chosen the latter. Their continuing choice provides the foundation or justification for much of the pervasive persecution and abuse of women throughout the world. This is in clear violation not just of the Universal Declaration of Human Rights but also the teachings of Jesus Christ, the Apostle Paul, Moses and the prophets, Muhammad, and founders of other great religions—all of whom have called for proper and equitable treatment of all the children of God. It is time we had the courage to challenge these views.<sup id="cite_ref-losing_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-losing-162"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In 2014, he published <i>A Call to Action: Women, Religion, Violence, and Power</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gun_control">Gun control</span></h3>
<p>Carter has publicly expressed support for assault weapons bans and background checks.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter090426_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter090426-164"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> In May 1994, Carter, along with former presidents <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">Gerald Ford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>, wrote to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">U.S. House of Representatives</a> in support of banning "semi-automatic assault guns."<sup id="cite_ref-Eaton940505_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eaton940505-165"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> In a February 2013 appearance on <a href="/wiki/Piers_Morgan_Tonight" title="Piers Morgan Tonight" class="mw-redirect">Piers Morgan Tonight</a>, Carter agreed that if the <a href="/wiki/Assault_Weapons_Ban_of_2013" title="Assault Weapons Ban of 2013">assault weapons ban</a> did not pass it would be mainly due to the <a href="/wiki/National_Rifle_Association" title="National Rifle Association">National Rifle Association</a> and its pressure on "weak-kneed" politicians.<sup id="cite_ref-Kurtz130222_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kurtz130222-166"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Race_in_politics">Race in politics</span></h3>
<p>Carter ignited debate in September 2009 when he stated, "I think an overwhelming portion of the intensely demonstrated animosity toward President Barack Obama is based on the fact that he is a black man, that he is African-American."<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> Obama disagreed with Carter's assessment. On CNN Obama stated, "Are there people out there who don't like me because of race? I'm sure there are&#160;... that's not the overriding issue here."<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Torture">Torture</span></h3>
<p>In a 2008 interview with <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>, Carter criticized the use of torture at <a href="/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay" title="Guantanamo Bay" class="mw-redirect">Guantanamo Bay</a>, saying that it "contravenes the basic principles on which this nation was founded."<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> He stated that the next President should make the promise that the United States will "never again torture a prisoner."<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JimmyCarteronBicycle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/JimmyCarteronBicycle.jpg/170px-JimmyCarteronBicycle.jpg" width="170" height="321" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/JimmyCarteronBicycle.jpg/255px-JimmyCarteronBicycle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/JimmyCarteronBicycle.jpg/340px-JimmyCarteronBicycle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="748" data-file-height="1413" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JimmyCarteronBicycle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Carter in Plains, 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Carter and his wife, <a href="/wiki/Rosalynn_Carter" title="Rosalynn Carter">Rosalynn</a>, are well known for their work as volunteers with <a href="/wiki/Habitat_for_Humanity" title="Habitat for Humanity">Habitat for Humanity</a>, a Georgia-based philanthropy that helps low-income working people around the world to build and buy their own homes and access clean water.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carter's hobbies include painting,<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fly-fishing" title="Fly-fishing" class="mw-redirect">fly-fishing</a>, woodworking, cycling, tennis, and skiing.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<p>From a young age, Carter showed a deep commitment to <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>. He teaches Sunday school and is a <a href="/wiki/Deacon" title="Deacon">deacon</a> at the Maranatha Baptist Church in his hometown of <a href="/wiki/Plains,_Georgia" title="Plains, Georgia">Plains</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Marantha_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marantha-176"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Marantha_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marantha-176"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> As president, Carter prayed several times a day, and professed that <a href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ" title="Jesus Christ" class="mw-redirect">Jesus Christ</a> was the driving force in his life. Carter had been greatly influenced by a sermon he had heard as a young man. It asked, "If you were arrested for being a Christian, would there be enough evidence to convict you?"<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The New York Times</i> noted that Carter had been instrumental in moving evangelical Christianity closer to the American mainstream during and after his presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2000, Carter severed his membership with the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a>, saying the group's doctrines did not align with his Christian beliefs. In April 2006, Carter, former President Bill Clinton, and Mercer University President Bill Underwood initiated the <a href="/wiki/New_Baptist_Covenant" title="New Baptist Covenant">New Baptist Covenant</a>. The broadly inclusive movement seeks to unite <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> of all races, cultures and convention affiliations. Eighteen Baptist leaders representing more than 20&#160;million Baptists across North America backed the group as an alternative to the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a>. The group held its first meeting in Atlanta, January 30 through February 1, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family">Family</span></h3>
<p>Carter had three younger siblings: sisters <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Carter_Spann" title="Gloria Carter Spann">Gloria Carter Spann</a> (1926–1990) and <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Carter_Stapleton" title="Ruth Carter Stapleton">Ruth Carter Stapleton</a> (1929–1983), and brother <a href="/wiki/Billy_Carter" title="Billy Carter">Billy Carter</a> (1937–1988).<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup> Cousins to Carter included politician <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Carter" title="Hugh Carter">Hugh Carter</a> and musician <a href="/wiki/June_Carter_Cash" title="June Carter Cash">June Carter Cash</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carter and <a href="/wiki/Rosalynn_Carter" title="Rosalynn Carter">Rosalynn Smith</a> were married in 1946. Together, they have three sons, one daughter, eight grandsons, three granddaughters, and two great-grandsons. They celebrated their 65th wedding anniversary in July 2011, making them the second-longest wed Presidential couple after <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Bush" title="Barbara Bush">Barbara Bush</a>. Prior to this milestone, their long-term marriage surpassed that of <a href="/wiki/John_Adams" title="John Adams">John</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abigail_Adams" title="Abigail Adams">Abigail Adams</a> on July 10, 2000. Their eldest son <a href="/wiki/Jack_Carter_(politician)" title="Jack Carter (politician)">Jack Carter</a> was the 2006 Democratic <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_election_in_Nevada,_2006" title="United States Senate election in Nevada, 2006">candidate for U.S. Senate</a> in Nevada before losing to the Republican incumbent, <a href="/wiki/John_Ensign" title="John Ensign">John Ensign</a>. Carter grandson <a href="/wiki/Jason_Carter_(politician)" title="Jason Carter (politician)">Jason Carter</a> is a former Georgia State Senator<sup id="cite_ref-NYTMay2010_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTMay2010-182"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> and in 2014 was the Democratic candidate for <a href="/wiki/Georgia_gubernatorial_election,_2014" title="Georgia gubernatorial election, 2014">governor of Georgia</a>, losing to the Republican incumbent, <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Deal" title="Nathan Deal">Nathan Deal</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cancer_diagnosis">Cancer diagnosis</span></h3>
<p>On August 3, 2015, Carter underwent elective surgery to remove "a small mass" on his <a href="/wiki/Liver" title="Liver">liver</a>, and his prognosis for a full recovery was initially said to be "excellent". On August 12, however, Carter announced he had been diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Metastatic_cancer" title="Metastatic cancer" class="mw-redirect">cancer that had spread elsewhere in his body</a>, without specifying where the cancer had originated.<sup id="cite_ref-cnbccancer_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnbccancer-183"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> On August 20, he disclosed that <a href="/wiki/Melanoma" title="Melanoma">melanoma</a> had been found in his brain and liver, and that he had begun treatment with the <a href="/wiki/Immunotherapy" title="Immunotherapy">immunotherapy</a> drug <a href="/wiki/Pembrolizumab" title="Pembrolizumab">pembrolizumab</a> and was about to start <a href="/wiki/Radiation_therapy" title="Radiation therapy">radiation therapy</a>. His healthcare is being managed by <a href="/wiki/Emory_Healthcare" title="Emory Healthcare">Emory Healthcare</a> of <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>. The former President has an extensive family history of cancer, including both of his parents and all three of his siblings.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Funeral_and_burial_plans">Funeral and burial plans</span></h3>
<p>Carter has planned to be buried in front of his home in Plains, Georgia. Carter noted in 2006 that a funeral in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> with visitation at the Carter Center was planned as well.<sup id="cite_ref-AP_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP-185"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_image_and_legacy">Public image and legacy</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
